The strategy to test the integrity of the code consisted of some test cases testing the following:

1) Valid inputs considering the pre-conditions.
2) Invalid inputs considering the pre-conditions

In the test_in1.txt, there are only valid elements. The handwritten calculation below illustrates what is expected to occur. First, we enumerated the test cases. Then, we enumerated books and page limits for each test case.
Then, sorted the array. There is a tracing illustrating what happened, and we counted how many books we could read in test case.

As expected, it matched. So, the first test case passed succesfully.

See below the calculations. 

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_in1.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3//Number of test cases
5 20 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 20
6 12 3 10 2 | Total pages of each book
5 21 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 21
12 3 6 10 2 | Total pages of each book
10 31 //Number of books in the school library: 10 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 31
9 6 6 3 8 2 12 15 13 7 | Total pages of each book

------------------------

The function process Case will process each case. It has passed (arr, 0, 5-1)

Test Case 1:

The array is: 6 12 3 10 2 

mid=(left+right)/2 -> mid=(0+4)/2 -> mid = 2

Then, it calls mergeSort(arr, 0, 2). After it processes all values and reach the base cases in this recursion, it will go to the next line to process mergeSort(arr, 3, 4) and merge(arr,0,2,3) that are waiting to start processing.
mergeSorts will divide the array, and the merge function will merge the parts together.

Essentially, this is a breakdown of what is happening in each step. Each number in parenthesis shows the order that each step occurred. 

						6 12 3 10 2 
						/  (1)   \
					    6 12 3 	10 2 
				     	/   (2)	|	 |(9)\
				     6 12       3        2    10 
				    /(3)|	|(7)	 \(10)/(11)	
				   6	12 		  2 10	
				   \(4) |(5)	|	   | (12)
			    	     6 12 	 				 
				      (6)\	|	   |	
					   3 6 12  			
						\(8)	   |
						  2 3 6 10 12  (13)

When the array is sorted in a non-decreasing order, we call the function maximumBooks passing the array of the test case, total books of the test case, and the page limit of the test case to find and display the maximum of books we can read.
This function considers the maximum of books read so far, the maximum of books available, maximum of pages read, the array, and the limit of pages of the test.
When it reaches the limit, it prints the number of books read.

In this casem the maximum of books is 5, and the maximum of pages is 20.

So, it will evaluate 2 considering all factors, and will add to to the maximum of pages read so far, and increase the books counter to 1.
Then, it will evaluate 2+3 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 20, it will add 2+3, and increase the books counter to 2.
Then, it will evaluate 5+6 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 20, it will add 5+6, and increase the books counter to 3.
Then, it will evaluate 11+10 considering the maximum of pages. As it is higher than 20, it will break the while loop, and print the maximum of books read 3.

The code matches the expectation. So, it is correct.

				Test Case#1: test_out1.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3
4
5

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

From the next cases on, I used a code to create test cases as it would be too exhaustive to write randomly generate the numbers. At a hightlevel, the code takes a lower and an upper bound to generate random numbers between that interval. 
These requirements ensure our input restrictions are maintained. I used loops to generate more than one number in case I had to generate multiple book pages.

In the test_in2.txt, we applied another valid input in the first test case. I had a test input file with a maximum page limit greater than 10^(10). The page limit set was 10000000001, which is 10^(10)+1.
As expected, the test passed.
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_in2.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3//Number of test cases
11 10000000001 //Number of books in the school library: 11 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 10^(10)+1
999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 12 | Total pages of each book
5 21 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 21
12 3 6 10 2 | Total pages of each book
10 31 //Number of books in the school library: 10 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 31
9 6 6 3 8 2 12 15 13 7 | Total pages of each book

The mergeSort and merge will perform exactly as in test_in1.txt, but using the numbers from test_in2.txt

The sorted array will look like this: 12 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999 999999999

When the array is sorted in a non-decreasing order, we call the function maximumBooks passing the array of the test case, total books of the test case, and the page limit of the test case to find and display the maximum of books we can read.
This function considers the maximum of books read so far, the maximum of books available, maximum of pages read, the array, and the limit of pages of the test.
When it reaches the limit, it prints the number of books read.

In this casem the maximum of books is 11, and the maximum of pages is 10^(10)+1.

So, it will evaluate 12 considering all factors, and will add to to the maximum of pages read so far, and increase the books counter to 1.
Then, it will evaluate 12+999999999  considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 12+999999999, and increase the books counter to 2.
Then, it will evaluate 1,000,000,011+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 1,000,000,011+999999999, and increase the books counter to 3.
Then, it will evaluate 2,000,000,010+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 2,000,000,010+999999999, and print the maximum of books read 4.
Then, it will evaluate 3,000,000,009+999999999  considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 3,000,000,009+999999999, and increase the books counter to 5.
Then, it will evaluate 4,000,000,008+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 4,000,000,008+999999999, and increase the books counter to 6.
Then, it will evaluate 5,000,000,007+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 5,000,000,007+999999999, and print the maximum of books read 7.
Then, it will evaluate 6,000,000,006+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 6,000,000,006+999999999, and print the maximum of books read 8.
Then, it will evaluate 7,000,000,005+999999999  considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 7,000,000,005+999999999, and increase the books counter to 9.
Then, it will evaluate 8,000,000,004+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is lower than 10^(10)+1, it will add 8,000,000,004+999999999, and increase the books counter to 10.
Then, it will evaluate 9,000,000,003+999999999 considering the maximum of pages. As it is higher than 10^(10)+1 because it is 10^(10)+2, it will break the while loop, and print the maximum of books read 10.

A similar process occurs for test cases 2 and 3. As expected they match, but the real test here was to evaluate the test case with a maximum page limit greater than 10^(10).

5 21 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 21
12 3 6 10 2
10 31 //Number of books in the school library: 10 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 31
9 6 6 3 8 2 12 15 13 7

The keys here were that no matter what it sorted, it would have only 1 page per book. The maximum of pages read would be a 100, so the maximum number of books read had to be 100!
As expected, it passed and the results matched. Check the test_out3.txt below.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_out3.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
100
4
5

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


In the test_in4.txt, we generatered according to the input restrictions random numbers in either maximum of pages and pages per book. Of course, I used the code mentioned above to generate these random numbers.
As expected, the test passed.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_in4.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
1 //Number of test cases
5 517960297 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 517960297 
28560263 825686973 130537059 99599033 535610216 

The sorted array will be: 28560263 99599033 130537059 535610216 825686973 

The sum of the first three elements is equals to 258,696,355. If we sum this number to the 4th element (535610216), it will result in 794,306,571. This number is greater than 517960297. So, the expected output is 3 as may be verified below.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_out4.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

In the test_in5.txt, we applied an invalid input to the total of pages of a book in the test case# 1. Number of pages is not valid. It should be a single positive integer between 1 and 10^(9), inclusive.
As expected, the test passed.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_in5.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
3 //Number of test cases
5 20 //Number of books in the school library: 5 | Maximum of pages we are willing to read: 20
1000000001 12 3 10 2 //pages per book expected to fail
5 21
12 3 6 10 2
10 31
9 6 6 3 8 2 12 15 13 7

The total of pages of the first book in the first test case is greater 10^(9) because it is 10^(9)+1. This test is expected to fail, and as may be verified in the test_out5.txt, it failed.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
				Test Case#1: test_out5.txt
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Number of pages is not valid. It should be a single positive integer between 1 and 10^(9), inclusive.

-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
